# Comments for Question 4, LLM=Grok 2 12-12

== Grader: Claude 3.7 Sonnet ==
  * grade_story_102.txt (grade=4.5)
    The story attempts symbolism with the dollhouse key representing possibility and the maps representing life paths, but these metaphors remain surface-level. The central conflict lacks urgency and specificity—what exactly is this prophecy and why must it be hushed? The theme of rediscovering courage has potential but is delivered through explicit telling rather than demonstrated through meaningful action. The ending feels predetermined rather than earned through character agency.

  * grade_story_0.txt (grade=4.5)
    The story attempts thematic depth with ideas about connection and understanding monsters, but these remain surface-level. The central conflict resolves too easily to create meaningful impact. The writing relies heavily on telling rather than showing, particularly regarding Eliot's emotions and the monster's reactions. Literary devices are minimal, and dialogue is absent, limiting the story's emotional resonance and depth.

  * grade_story_1.txt (grade=3.5)
    The story relies heavily on telling rather than showing, particularly regarding Alex's emotional journey. Phrases like "felt a surge of exhilaration" and "had found a new sense of freedom" state emotions without demonstrating them through action or specific detail. The metaphor of unraveling knots as conquering fears is obvious rather than nuanced. The ending feels rushed and overly explanatory, spelling out the story's message rather than allowing readers to discover it.

  * grade_story_103.txt (grade=3.5)
    The story relies heavily on telling rather than showing, with emotions explicitly stated ("joyful agony," "heart torn") rather than demonstrated through action. The central conflict remains abstract, and the ending withholds resolution, leaving readers without satisfaction or meaningful reflection. While there's an attempt at creating mystery, the lack of concrete details about what lies behind the door diminishes emotional impact. The writing employs repetitive phrasing and lacks distinctive style.
